Revision: 58519
Author: michaelp
Date: Friday, March 02, 2012 2:21:25 PM
Message:
- Enhanced GUIBitmapButtonCtrl to give a user more control over image selection for the button states.

New fields:
isLegacyVersion - Determines if this is a legacy version of the control (only uses bitmap field)
bitmapNormal - Name of texture used for the normal button state
bitmapHilight - Name of texture used for the hilight/hover button state
bitmapDepressed  -  Name of texture used for the depressed button state
bitmapInactive - Name of texture used for the inactive button state
As you can guess, this allows you to now specify an individual image for each state without having to use the underscore naming scheme.

New Methods:
setBitmapNormal (filepath name) - Loads a bitmap from a given file for the "up" state
setBitmapHilight (filepath name) - Loads a bitmap from a given file for the "down" state
setBitmapDepressed (filepath name) - Loads a bitmap from a given file for the "hover" state
setBitmapInactive (filepath name) - Loads a bitmap from a given file for the "inactive" state

Backwards compatibility has been maintained, so any GUIs using the bitmap field and setBitmap function should still work. For the template editors that allow a user to select an image for each button, make sure you do the following:

1. Set isLegacyVersion to false or 0
2. Remove bitmap field. Replace with bitmapNormal, bitmapHilight, bitmapDepressed, and bitmapInactive
3. Remove any instances of setBitmap in your code. Replace with the new methods.
----

Revision: 57846
Author: Melv_May
Date: Monday, February 20, 2012 4:46:43 AM
Message:
- Added more functionality to NameTags:

Single object helpers:
> tag
> untag
> hasTag

Multi-object query:
> queryTags

Simple added any objects you wish to the NameTags (it's a SimSet now) and when using "quertTags", it'll search all those objects for you which is much faster than iterating using TS.

Use the single object helpers to add/remove and check for the presence of tags on individual objects.  This uses a hard-wired field name of "NameTags" to perform the operations.

All the above methods allow the specification of multiple tags if required.
